## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (deterministic rate-law ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard setting of chemical kinetics modeled by ordinary differential equations. With only (t, A) available, the likely structures are single-species rate laws (various reaction orders), approach-to-equilibrium forms, and time-varying effective rate constants representing changing conditions (temperature, light, catalyst activity, feed).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when reactant is in excess or rate-limited by a constant flux)
- Zero-order production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate generation due to constant feed/source)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or effective second-order loss)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global order kinetics for complex mechanisms)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (linear): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to deviation from equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating with limiting term: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis or limited-capacity growth/decay in a closed system)
- Source-plus-decay (CSTR-like lumped model): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant inflow/production balanced by first-order loss)
- Time-ramped rate constant: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (effective rate changes linearly in time due to controlled ramping/aging)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (light/temperature modulation or cyclic operation)
- Catalyst deactivation / activity decay: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (rate proportional to decaying catalyst activity)
- Diffusion/transport-limited effective rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / ((t + c1)**c2) (apparent rate decreases with time due to boundary-layer growth or depletion effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (a straight line in dA_dt vs A at fixed conditions), it suggests first-order kinetics (unimolecular or pseudo-first-order).
- If dA_dt scales like A**2 or higher powers, it indicates higher molecularity steps or effective global reaction order from a mechanism lumping.
- A factor of (A - c) implies approach to an equilibrium/steady concentration c (reversible reaction or balance of production and loss).
- A product A*(c - A) suggests self-acceleration at low A with a built-in upper bound (autocatalysis with depletion/limited capacity).
- Explicit time dependence in the coefficient multiplying A (e.g., c0 + c1*t or sin(c*t)) points to changing external conditions (temperature/light/operation cycles) rather than intrinsic concentration-only kinetics.
- A multiplicative exp(-c*t) on the rate indicates decaying activity (catalyst deactivation, fouling, poisoning) superimposed on intrinsic kinetics.
- An additive constant term in dA_dt (e.g., +c0) indicates a source/feed term independent of A (injection, inflow, background generation).
- A rate that weakens with time via division by (t+c)**p is characteristic of transport limitations or progressive accessibility loss (diffusion boundary layer, passivation).
